.. _s.Life2550:

Tree of Life, 2550 taxa
***********************

One-per-species tree of life, made from the completed and draft
genomes available on 1 April, 2013, in :download:`phyloxml format
<dl/Life2550.phyloxml>`.

.. figure:: images/fig_tree.png
   :width: 70%

In order to provide correspondence to NCBI's taxonomy and the
reference genomes, this chapter presents the list of reference genomes
linked to NCBI on the basis of genus and species names.  The complete
directory name from the NCBI ftp site also appears below, and the
combination allows the current release of each genome to be located.

Sequedex was `developed
<http://www.biomedcentral.com/1756-0500/5/460/abstract>`_ with a
signature list and phylogenetic classification based on a bacterial
one-per-genus tree of 403 taxa.  Since that time, we have increased
both the breadth and resolution of this tree to include bacteria,
archaea, and eukaryotes at the one-per-species resolution.  The tree
was based on an amino acid alignment of the concatenated RNA
polymerase beta and beta prime subunits (for bacteria) or the
analogous subunits of RNA pol II (for eukaryotes).

Phylogenetic information can be visualized in a variety of ways, and
this chapter attempts to start the user with phylum-level,
family-level, and species-level identifications of what is present in
a sample.  Although labeled as phylum and family, we took liberties in
using the pair of classifications that best suited the density of
reference genomes in each region of the phylogeny, to obtain a
labeling scheme that is parsimonious, spanning, and non-overlapping.
By clicking on the taxon names, the user can easily compare to all
levels of the taxonomy assigned by NCBI.

As described in the Introduction, Sequedex captures the uncertainty
inherent in classifying fragments of DNA by making phylogenetic
assignments to the nodes of a binary phylogenetic tree, and not to
individual taxa.  Consequently, some node numbers are indicative of
phyla, some nodes are indicative of families, and some are specific to
a pair of taxa.  In the table below, we provide all three types of
information.  Because of the way the nodes on the trees were numbered,
through a depth-first traversal, node numbers intermediate between
these two extremes are intermediate nodes between the group name
(family or phylum) and the leaves.  PDF files are available with
page-sized chunks of the tree throughout the tree, and are indicated
at the beginning of each section, :ref:`s.Bacteroidetes`,
:ref:`s.aprot`, :ref:`s.bgprot`, :ref:`s.actinobacteria`,
:ref:`s.firmicutes`, :ref:`s.cyanobacteria`, :ref:`s.archaea`, and
:ref:`s.euks`.

There are undoubtably minor mistakes in this classification.  The nature of
the signature peptide method, however, is such that these mistakes
serve to bluzrr out phylogenetic signals, not result in spurious
assignments to specific nodes.

.. _s.Bacteroidetes:

Bacteroidetes, et al.
=====================

This group contains Chlamydia, Verrucomicrobia, Planctomycetes,
Spirochaetes, Fusobacteria, Elusimicrobia, Gemmatimonads,
Salinibacter, Chlorobia, Cytophaga, Pedobacteria,Flavobacteria, and
bacteroidetes.  Annotated pdfs with node numbers and family names are
available for:

*    :download:`spirochaetes + fusobacteria <dl/Spiro_fuso.pdf>`, 
*    :download:`bacteroidetes <dl/Bacteroidetes.pdf>`, 
*    :download:`chlamydia + verrucomicrobia + planctomycetes <dl/Chlam_planct.pdf>`, 
*    and :download:`chlorobi <dl/Chlorobi.pdf>`.

.. _s.aprot:

Alpha proteobacteria, et al.
============================

This group contains Helicobacter, Campylobacter, Acidobacteriales, Aquificae, Deferribacteria, Desulfovibriales, Desulfotaleales, Myxococcus, Gebacteriales, Rhizobia, Caulobacteriales, Rhodobacteria, Sphingomonads, Rickettesia, Rhodospirilliae.
PDFs are available for:

*   :download:`Delta, Epsilon Proteobacteria, Aquificae, Acidobacteria, and others <dl/deprot.pdf>`.
*   Alpha Proteobacteria, part 1, including :download:`Rickettsiales and Rhodospirillales <dl/aprot1.pdf>`.
*   Alpha Proteobacteria, part 2, including :download:`Sphingomonadales and Rhodobacteraceae <dl/aprot2.pdf>`.

.. _s.bgprot:

Beta and Gamma Proteobacteria
=============================

This group contains Enteric, Haemophilus, Vibrio, Shewanella, Pseudomonads, Coxiella, Thiomicrospira, Nitrosococcus, Xanthomonads, Methylobacteria, Acidothiobacillus, Francisella, Neisseria, Burkholderiales, Azoarcus, Thiobacillus.

*  Gamma proteobacteria 1, including :download:`Enterobacteriales, Vibrionales, Alteromonadales, Shewanellaceae, and others <dl/gprot1.pdf>`
*  Gamma proteobacteria 2, including :download:`Pseudomonadales, Moraxellaceae, Oceanospirillales, Xanthomonadales, and others <dl/gprot2.pdf>`
*  :download:`Beta proteobacteria <dl/bprot.pdf>`.

.. _s.actinobacteria:

Actinobacteria
==============

This group contains Rubrobacteria, Slackia, Acidothermus, Streptomyces, and Nocardia

*   Actinobacteria group 1, including :download:`Coriobacteriales, Micrococcinea, and Bifidobacteriaea <dl/Actinobacteria1.pdf>`, 
*   Actinobacteria group 2, including :download:`Corynebacterineae, Nocardiaceae, and Frankiaceae <dl/Actinobacteria2.pdf>`,

.. _s.firmicutes:

Firmicutes, et al.
==================

This group contains Thermotogae, Dictyoglomus, Thermoanaerovibrio, Deinococcus/Thermus, Chloroflexi, Syntrophomonads, Selenomonads, Bacilli, Lactobacilli, Mycoplasmas, and Clostridia.  Annotated pdfs with node numbers are available for:

*   :download:`Deinococcus+Thermotogae+Synergistetes+Chloroflexi <dl/Deino+Chloroflexi.pdf>`, 
*   Clostridia part 1 :download:`(Clostridiaceae, Ruminococcaceae, Eubacteriaceae) <dl/Clostridia1.pdf>`, 
*   Clostridia part 2 :download:`(Negativicutes, Peptococcaceae, Halanaerobales) <dl/Clostridia2.pdf>`, 
*   :download:`Lactobacillales <dl/Lactobacillales.pdf>`, 
*   :download:`Bacillales <dl/Bacillales.pdf>`, and 
*   :download:`Eryspelotrichi+Mollicutes <dl/Erys+Mollicutes.pdf>`.

Family names and links to Genbank are below.

.. _s.cyanobacteria:

Cyanobacteria
=============

This group contains Cyanobacteria.  An annotated pdf with node numbers is available for

*   :download:`Cyanobacteria <dl/Cyanobacteria.pdf>`.

  For a recent discussion of the cyanobacterial phylogeny, please see Shih, et al., `Improving the coverage of the cyanobacterial phylum using diversity-driven genome sequencing. <http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/23277585>`_

.. _s.archaea:

Archaea
=============

This group contains the Archaea.  Annotated pdfs with node numbers and family names are available for 

*   :download:`crenarchaeota <dl/Crenarchaeota.pdf>` and 
*   :download:`euryarchaeota <dl/Euryarchaeota.pdf>`.

Jump to: :ref:`s.Bacteroidetes`, :ref:`s.aprot`, :ref:`s.bgprot`, :ref:`s.actinobacteria`, :ref:`s.firmicutes`, :ref:`s.cyanobacteria`, :ref:`s.archaea`, and :ref:`s.euks`.

.. _s.euks:

Eukaryotes
=============

This group contains the the Eukaryotes.  Annotated pdfs with node numbers and family names are available for download for

*   :download:`plants and protozoa <dl/Plants_protists.pdf>` and 
*   :download:`Metazoa and fungi <dl/Metazoa_fungi.pdf>`.  

The phylogeny of lower eukaryotes is significantly more difficult to understand than the rest of this tree, and we relied heavily on `Ginger, et al. <http://rstb.royalsocietypublishing.org/content/365/1541/693.full>`_, `Koonin <http://genomebiology.com/2010/11/5/209>`_, and `Adl, et al. <http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/23020233>`_ in assembling this phylogeny.
